/rɪˈpeə(r) ||; rɪˈpɛr/noun [C,U] something that you do to fix sth that is damaged 修理；修补: The school is closed for repairs to the roof. 学校现已关闭，以便修理屋顶。 The road is in need of repair. 这条路需要维修。 The bridge is under repair. 那座桥正在维修中。 The bike was damaged beyond repair so I threw it away. 那辆自行车损坏得无法修理了，所以我把它扔掉了。 in good, bad, etc repair in a good, bad, etc condition 保养良好╱不善等

/ˌrepəˈreɪʃn ||; ˌrɛpəˈreʃən/noun (formal 正式)

repay
/rɪˈpeɪ ||; rɪˈpe/verb [T] (past tense past participle repaid /rɪˈpeɪd ||; rɪˈped/)
1 repay sth (to sb);repay (sb) sth to pay back money that you owe to sb 付还，偿还（欠款）: to repay a debt/loan 偿还债务╱贷款 When will you repay the money to them? 你什么时候把这笔钱还给他们？ When will you repay them the money? 你什么时候还给他们这笔钱？
2 repay sb (for sth) to give sth to sb in return for help, kindness, etc 报答；回报: How can I ever repay you for all you have done for me? 我怎样才能报答你为我所做的一切呢？

*repeat¹
/rɪˈpi:t ||; rɪˈpit/verb
1 [I,T] repeat (sth/yourself) to say, write or do sth again or more than once 重说；重写；重做；重复 · Don't repeat the same mistake again. 不要重蹈覆辙。 Could you repeat what you just said? 你可以重复一下你刚才说的话吗？ The essay is quite good, but you repeat yourself several times. 你这篇文章不错，但有数处重复。 Raise and lower your left leg ten times, then repeat with the right. 将左腿抬起、放下十次，然后用右腿重复这一动作。
2 [T] repeat sth (to sb) to say or write sth that sb else has said or written or that you have learnt 复述；把（听到、看到或学到的）说出来或写下来: Please don't repeat what you've heard here to anyone. 请不要把你在这里听到的事对任何人说。 Repeat each sentence after me. 跟着我念每个句子。 ☞noun repetition 名词为repetition

/rɪˈpi:t ||; rɪˈpit/noun [C] something that is done, shown, given, etc again 重复做的事: I think I've seen this programme before -- it must be a repeat. 这个节目我觉得以前看过，一定是回放的。

repeated
/rɪˈpi:tɪd ||; rɪˈpitɪd/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) done or happening many times 重复的；反复发生的: There have been repeated accidents on this stretch of road. 这段路经常出事。 ➔repeatedly adv I've asked him repeatedly not to leave his bicycle there. 我三番两次叫他不要把自行车放在那里。

repellent²

repent
/rɪˈpent ||; rɪˈpɛnt/verb [I,T] (formal 正式)repent (sth);repent of sth to feel and show that you are sorry about sth bad that you have done 悔悟；悔改 [I] to repent of your sins 为罪过忏悔 He repented his hasty decision. 他后悔做出仓促的决定。 ➔repentance noun [U] /-əns ||; -əns/ ➔repentant /-ənt ||; -ənt/ adj

repertoire
/ˈrepətwɑ:(r) ||; ˈrɛpɚˌtwɑr/noun[C]

2 all the things that a person is able to do （一个人的）全部本领

repetition
/ˌrepəˈtɪʃn ||; ˌrɛpɪˈtɪʃən/noun [U] [C] doing sth again; sth that you do or that happens again 重复；重复做或发生的事: to learn by repetition 反复学习 Let's try to avoid a repetition of what happened last Friday. 我们要尽量避免上星期五所发生的事情重演。 ☞verb repeat 动词为repeat

repetitive
/rɪˈpetətɪv ||; rɪˈpɛtɪtɪv/ (also repetitious /ˌrepəˈtɪʃəs ||; ˌrɛpɪˈtɪʃəs/) adj not interesting because the same thing is repeated many times 重复而没有变化的

*replace
/rɪˈpleɪs ||; rɪˈples/verb[T]
1 replace sb/sth (as/with sb/sth) to take the place of sb/sth; to use sb/sth in place of another person or thing 取代；代替: Teachers will never be replaced by computers in the classroom. 在课堂里，老师永远也不会被计算机所替代。
2 replace sb/sth (with sb/sth) to exchange sb/sth for sb/sth that is better or newer 更换；换成好的或新的；调换: We will replace any goods that are damaged. 我们会更换任何损坏的货物。
3 to put sth back in the place where it was before 放回原处: Please replace the books on the shelves when you have finished with them. 那些书看完后，请放回书架上。 ☞ Put back is more common and less formal. put back较常用，多用于非正式场合。

replaceable
/rɪˈpleɪsəbl ||; rɪˈplesəbḷ/adj that can be replaced 可更换的；可替换的 [OPP] irreplaceable 反义词为irreplaceable

replacement
/rɪˈpleɪsmənt ||; rɪˈplesmənt/noun
1 [U] exchanging sb/sth for sb/sth that is better or newer 更换；调换；替换: The carpets are in need of replacement. 这些地毯需要更换。
2 [C] a person or thing that will take the place of sb/sth 接替者；代替物: Mary is leaving next month so we must advertise for a replacement for her. 玛丽将于下个月离职，我们必须登广告招聘人接替她。

replay¹
/ˈri:pleɪ ||; ˈriˌple/noun[C]
1 (Brit 英) a sports match that is played again because neither team won the first time 重赛（因为第一次难分胜负）
2 something on the television, on a film or a cassette tape that you watch or listen to again 回放；重放: Now let's see an action replay of that tremendous goal! 现在让我们来看看那精彩入球动作的回放！
replay²
/ˌri:ˈpleɪ ||; riˈple/verb[T]
1 to play a sports match, etc again because neither team won the first time 重赛（因第一次难分胜负）
2 to play again sth that you have recorded 回放；重放: They kept replaying the goal over and over again. 他们反复地回放那个入球动作。

*reply
/rɪˈplaɪ ||; rɪˈplaɪ/verb [I,T] (present participle replying third person singular present replies;past tense past participle replied)reply (to sb/sth) (with sth) to say, write or do sth as an answer to sb/sth 回答；答复: I wrote to Sue but she hasn't replied. 我写信给休，但她没有回复。 ‘Yes, I will,’ she replied. “是呀，我会的。”她答道。 [I] to reply to a question 回答问题 ☞Look at the note at answer ¹. 参看answer^1的注释。 reply noun [C,U] (plural replies) Al nodded in reply to my question. 对于我的问题，阿尔点头响应。

*report¹
/rɪˈpɔ:t ||; rɪˈpɔrt/verb
1 [I,T] report (on sb/sth) (to sb/sth);report sth (to sb) to give people information about what you have seen, heard, done, etc 报告；汇报 · Several people reported seeing/having seen the boy. 几个人说曾经见过那男孩。 Several people reported that they had seen the boy. 几个人说他们曾经见过那男孩。 The company reported huge profits last year. 这家公司报告说，去年有巨额利润。 Call me if you have anything new to report. 如果你有什么新情况向我报告，就给我打电话。
2 [I,T] report (on) sth (in a newspaper or on the television or radio) to write or speak about sth that has happened （报纸、电视或电台）报道: The paper sent a journalist to report on the events. 这家报纸派了一名记者去报道那些活动。
3 [T] report sb (to sb) (for sth) to tell a person in authority about an accident, a crime, etc or about sth wrong that sb has done （向当局）报告（事故等）；报案；告发 · All accidents must be reported to the police. 一切事故都必须报告警方。 The boy was reported missing early this morning. 据报告，该男孩于今天清晨失踪。
4 [I] report (to sb/sth) for sth to tell sb that you have arrived 报到: On your arrival, please report to the reception desk. 你抵达后，请到服务台报到。
5 [T] (formal 正式)be reported to be/as sth used to say that you have heard sth said, but you are not sure if it is true 据说: The 70-year-old actor is reported to be/as being comfortable in hospital. 据说，那位70岁的演员已安然住进医院。
report back (on sth) (to sb) to give information to sb about sth that he/she has asked you to find out about （按要求）报告，回报: One person in each group will then report back to the class on what you've decided. 然后，每一组派一人向全班报告所做的决定。 report to sb (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to have sb as your manager in the company or organization that you work for 隶属（某人） Although this verb is not used in the continuous tenses, it is common to see the present participle (= -ing form) A new team was put together for the project, reporting to Michael Nolan. 虽然这个动词不用于进行时，但它的现在分词还是常见：A new team was put together for the project, reporting to Michael Nolan.一个新的班子组建起来负责该工程，以迈克尔．诺兰为经理。
 *report²
/rɪˈpɔ:t ||; rɪˈpɔrt/noun[C]
1 a report (on/of sth) a written or spoken description of what you have seen, heard, done, studied, etc 报告；报道: newspaper reports 新闻报道 a report on the company's finances 公司的财务报告 a first-hand report (= from the person who saw what happened) 第一手报道
2 a written statement about the work of a student at school, college, etc 成绩（报告）单: to get a good/bad report 取得好╱坏成绩

reportedly
/rɪˈpɔ:tɪdli ||; rɪˈpɔrtɪdlɪ/adv (written 书面语) according to what some people say 据说；据报道: The band have reportedly decided to split up. 据说该乐队已决定解散。

reporter
/rɪˈpɔ:tə(r) ||; rɪˈpɔrtɚ/noun [C] a person who writes about the news in a newspaper or speaks about it on the television or radio 新闻记者；新闻报道员 ☞Look at journalist. 参看journalist。

*represent
/ˌreprɪˈzent ||; ˌrɛprɪˈzɛnt/verb
1 [T] to act or speak in the place of sb else; to be the representative of a group or country 代表；作为（一个群体或国家的）代表: You will need a lawyer to represent you in court. 你需要一位律师在庭上替你辩护。 It's an honour for an athlete to represent his or her country. 能代表自己国家参加比赛是运动员的光荣。
2 linking verb to be equal to sth; to be sth 相当于: These results represent a major breakthrough in our understanding of cancer. 这些成果意味着我们对癌症的认识取得了重大突破。
3 [T] to be a picture, sign, example, etc of sb/sth 代表；表示；象征: The yellow lines on the map represent minor roads. 地图上的黄线代表小路。
4 [T] to describe sb/sth in a particular way （以某方式）描述，描写

*representation
/ˌreprɪzenˈteɪʃn ||; ˌrɛprɪzɛnˈteʃən/noun
1 [U] [C] the way that sb/sth is shown or described; something that shows or describes sth 表示；表现；表示或表现某人或某事物的东西: The article complains about the representation of women in advertising. 这篇文章对广告中呈现的妇女形象感到不满。
2 [U] (formal 正式) having sb to speak for you 代表 ☞Look at proportional representation. 参看proportional representation。

representative¹
/ˌreprɪˈzentətɪv ||; ˌrɛprɪˈzɛntətɪv/adj representative (of sb/sth) typical of a larger group to which sb/sth belongs 典型的；有代表性的: Tonight's audience is not representative of national opinion. 今晚的听众不能代表全国的意见。
representative²
/ˌreprɪˈzentətɪv ||; ˌrɛprɪˈzɛntətɪv/noun[C]
1 a person who has been chosen to act or speak for sb else or for a group 代表
2 (formal 正式)=REP

repress
/rɪˈpres ||; rɪˈprɛs/verb[T]
1 to control an emotion or to try to prevent it from being shown or felt 压抑，抑制（感情）: She tried to repress her anger. 她努力抑制怒气。
2 to limit the freedom of a group of people 限制（某一群人的）自由 ➔repression /rɪˈpreʃn ||; rɪˈprɛʃən/ noun [U]: protests against government repression 反对政府压制的抗议活动

repressed
/rɪˈprest ||; rɪˈprɛst/adj
1 (used about a person) having emotions and desires that he/she does not show or express （指人）受压抑的
2 (used about an emotion) that you do not show （指情绪）潜藏的: repressed anger/desire 潜藏的愤怒╱欲望

repressive
/rɪˈpresɪv ||; rɪˈprɛsɪv/adj that limits people's freedom 限制人身自由的；压制的: a repressive government 采取高压手段的政府

reprieve
/rɪˈpri:v ||; rɪˈpriv/verb [T] to stop or delay the punishment of a prisoner who was going to be punished by death 缓期执行死刑；暂缓处决 reprieve noun [C]: The judge granted him a last-minute reprieve. 法官在最后一分钟准他缓期处决。

reprimand
/ˈreprɪmɑ:nd; US -mænd ||; ˈrɛprəˌmænd/verb [T] reprimand sb (for sth) to tell sb officially that he/she has done sth wrong 谴责；斥责 reprimand noun [C]: a severe reprimand 严厉的谴责

reprisal
/rɪˈpraɪzl ||; rɪˈpraɪzḷ/noun [C,U] punishment, especially by military force, for harm that one group of people does to another 报复（尤指军事的）

reproach
/rɪˈprəʊtʃ ||; rɪˈprotʃ/verb [T] reproach sb (for/with sth) to tell sb that he/she has done sth wrong; to blame sb 责备；指责；归咎于: You've nothing to reproach yourself for. It wasn't your fault. 你无须自责，这不是你的错。 reproach noun [C,U] His behaviour is beyond reproach (= cannot be criticized). 他的行为十分得体，无懈可击。 Alison felt his reproaches were unjustified. 艾莉森认为他的指责是没有根据的。 ➔reproachful /-fl ||; -fəl/ adj a reproachful look 责备的神情 ➔reproachfully /-fəli ||; -fəlɪ/ adv

*reproduce
/ˌri:prəˈdju:s; US -ˈdu:s ||; ˌriprəˈdus/verb
1 [T] to produce a copy of sth 复制；仿制: It is very hard to reproduce a natural environment in the laboratory. 在实验室内很难模拟大自然环境。
2 [I] (used about people, animals and plants) to produce young （指人、动物及植物）繁殖，生殖

*reproduction
/ˌri:prəˈdʌkʃn ||; ˌriprəˈdʌkʃən/noun
1 [U] the process of producing babies or young 繁殖；生殖: sexual reproduction 有性生殖
2 [U] the production of copies of sth 复制: Digital recording gives excellent sound reproduction. 数字式录音的录音效果极佳。
3 [C] a copy of a painting, etc 复制品；仿制品

reproductive
/ˌri:prəˈdʌktɪv ||; ˌriprəˈdʌktɪv/adj connected with the production of young animals, plants, etc 繁殖的；生殖的: the male reproductive organs 雄性生殖器官

reproof
/rɪˈpru:f ||; rɪˈpruf/noun [C,U] (formal 正式) something that you say to sb when you do not approve of what he/she has done 斥责；责备；非难

reptile
/ˈreptaɪl; US -tl ||; ˈrɛptḷ/noun [C] an animal that has cold blood and a skin covered in scales, and whose young come out of eggs, for example CROCODILES and snakes 爬行动物，爬虫类（如鳄鱼和蛇） ☞Compare amphibian. 与amphibian比较。

*republic
/rɪˈpʌblɪk ||; rɪˈpʌblɪk/noun [C] a country that has an elected government and an elected leader (president) 共和国: the Republic of Ireland 爱尔兰共和国 ☞Look at monarchy. 参看monarchy。

republican
/rɪˈpʌblɪkən ||; rɪˈpʌblɪkən/noun[C]
1 a person who supports the system of an elected government and leader 支持共和政体的人；共和主义者
2 Republican a member of the Republican Party 共和党员 ☞Look at Democrat. 参看Democrat。 republican adj

repudiate
/rɪˈpju:dieɪt ||; rɪˈpjudɪˌet/verb [T] to say that you refuse to accept or believe sth 拒绝接受；拒绝承认: to repudiate a suggestion/an accusation/responsibility 拒不接受建议；否认指控；拒绝承担责任 ➔repudiation /rɪˌpju:diˈeɪʃn ||; rɪˌpjudɪˈeʃən/ noun [U]

repugnant
/rɪˈpʌgnənt ||; rɪˈpʌgnənt/adj (not usually before a noun 通常不用于名词前) (formal 正式)repugnant (to sb) making you feel disgust 令人反感或厌恶: We found his suggestion absolutely repugnant. 我们觉得他的建议极其令人反感。 The idea of eating meat was repugnant to her. 她一想到吃肉就很反感。

repulse
/rɪˈpʌls ||; rɪˈpʌls/verb [T] (formal 正式)
1 to fight sb who is attacking you and drive him/her away 击退；打垮；驱逐: to repulse an attack/invasion/offensive 击退一次进攻/入侵/攻势
2 to refuse to accept sb's help, attempts to be friendly, etc 拒绝接受；回绝: She repulsed his advances. 她拒绝了他的追求。
3 (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) to make sb feel disgust or strong dislike 使厌恶；使反感: I was repulsed by the horrible smell. 这种可怕的气味让我恶心。

repulsion
/rɪˈpʌlʃn ||; rɪˈpʌlʃən/noun[U]
1 a strong feeling of not liking sth that you find extremely unpleasant 反感；厌恶
2 the force by which objects push each other away 排斥力；斥力: the forces of attraction and repulsion 吸引力与排斥力 ☞verb repel 动词为repel ☞picture at magnet 见magnet插图

repulsive
/rɪˈpʌlsɪv ||; rɪˈpʌlsɪv/adj that causes a strong feeling of disgust 令人讨厌或反感的 ☞verb repel 动词为repel ➔repulsion noun [U]

reputable
/ˈrepjətəbl ||; ˈrɛpjətəbḷ/adj that is known to be good 声誉良好的 [OPP] disreputable 反义词为disreputable

*reputation
/ˌrepjuˈteɪʃn ||; ˌrɛpjəˈteʃən/noun [C] a reputation (for/as sth) the opinion that people in general have about what sb/sth is like 名誉；名声；声誉: to have a good / bad reputation 名誉好╱坏 Adam has a reputation for being late. 亚当迟到出了名。 [SYN] name 同义词为name

repute
/rɪˈpju:t ||; rɪˈpjut/noun [U] (formal 正式) the opinion that people have of sb/sth 名声；名气: I know him only by repute. 我只知道他的名气。 She is a writer of international repute. 她是个在国际上有名气的作家。 [SYN] reputation 同义词为reputation

reputed
/rɪˈpju:tɪd ||; rɪˈpjutɪd/adj generally said to be sth, although it is not certain 被普遍认为的（并非一定符合事实）；据说是: He's reputed to be the highest-paid sportsman in the world. 人们普遍认为他是世界上薪金最高的运动员。 ➔reputedly adv

*request¹
/rɪˈkwest ||; rɪˈkwɛst/noun [C,U] request (for sth/that...) an act of asking for sth 要求；请求: a request for help 要求帮助 I'm going to make a request for a larger desk. 我打算要一张大一点的办公桌。 to grant/turn down a request 答应╱拒绝一个请求 Single rooms are available on request. 备有单人房，如有需要，可作安排。
request²
/rɪˈkwest ||; rɪˈkwɛst/verb [T] (formal 正式)request sth (from/of sb) to ask for sth 要求；请求: Passengers are requested not to smoke on this bus. 乘客请勿在公共汽车内吸烟。 to request a loan from the bank 向银行申请贷款 ☞ Request is more formal than ask. 与ask相比，request多用于正式场合。

/rekwiəm ||; ˈrɛkwɪəm/ (also ˌrequiem ˈmass) noun [C]

*require
/rɪˈkwaɪə(r) ||; rɪˈkwaɪr/verb[T]
1 to need sth 需要: a situation that requires tact and diplomacy 需要圆通技巧及外交手腕来处理的局面 ☞ Require is more formal than need. 与need相比，require多用于正式场合。
2 (often passive 常用于被动语态) to officially demand or order sth 规定；命令: Passengers are required by law to wear seat belts. 乘客必须依法系上安全带。

requirement
/rɪˈkwaɪəmənt ||; rɪˈkwaɪrmənt/noun [C] something that you need or that you must do or have 需要；要求；规定: university entrance requirements 大学入学条件

requisite
/ˈrekwɪzɪt ||; ˈrɛkwəzɪt/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) (formal 正式) necessary for a particular purpose 必要的；必不可少的: She lacks the requisite experience for the job. 她缺少必要的经验，不能胜任这项工作。 ➔requisite noun [C]: a requisite (for/of sth) toilet requisites 卫生间的必需品 A university degree has become a requisite for entry into most professions. 大学学位已经成为进入大多数专业的必要条件。 ☞Look at prerequisite. 参看prerequisite。

*research

reservation

*reserve¹
/rɪˈzɜ:v ||; rɪˈzɝv/verb [T] reserve sth (for sb/sth)
1 to keep sth for a special reason or to use at a later time 预留；保留: The car park is reserved for hotel guests only. 停车场只供饭店的顾客使用。
2 to ask for a seat, table, room, etc to be available at a future time; to book 预订（座位、桌子、房间等）: to reserve theatre tickets 预订戏票
reserve²
/rɪˈzɜ:v ||; rɪˈzɝv/noun
1 [C] [usu.pl] something that you keep for a special reason or to use at a later date 储存备用之物；储备: The US has huge oil reserves. 美国有庞大的石油储备。
2 [C] an area of land where the plants, animals, etc are protected by law 保护区（区内的动植物等均受法律保护）: a nature reserve 自然保护区 He works as a warden on a game reserve in Kenya. 他在肯尼亚野生动物保护区当管理员。
3 [U] the quality of being shy or keeping your feelings hidden 含蓄；克制；矜持；拘谨: It took a long time to break down her reserve and get her to relax. 花了很长时间才使她不再拘谨，放松下来。
4 [C] (in sport) a person who will play in a game if one of the usual members of the team cannot play （体育）替补、后补或预备队员，后备
in reserve that you keep and do not use unless you need to 储备；备用: Keep some money in reserve for emergencies. 要留下一点钱以应不时之需。

reset
/ˌri:ˈset ||; riˈsɛt/verb [T] (present participle resetting; past tense, past participle reset)

resettle
/ˌri:ˈsetl ||; riˈsɛtḷ/verb[I,T]
1 to help people go and live in a new country or area; to go and live in a new country or area 帮助…定居他国﹙或其他地区﹚；到他国﹙或其他地区﹚定居: Many of the refugees were resettled in Britain and Canada. 许多难民得到了帮助，得以在英国和加拿大定居。

residency

*resident

residential
/ˌrezɪˈdenʃl ||; ˌrɛzəˈdɛnʃəl/adj
1 (used about a place or an area) that has houses rather than offices, large shops or factories （指地方或地区）以住宅为主的: They live in a quiet residential area. 他们住在一个幽静的住宅区。
2 that provides a place for sb to live 居住的；家居的: This home provides residential care for the elderly. 这家疗养院为老人提供住宿护理。

residual
/rɪˈzɪdjuəl ||; rɪˈzɪdʒυəl/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) (formal 正式) left at the end of a process 残留的；剩下的: There are still a few residual problems with the computer program. 这计算机程序还有几个问题没有解决。

residue
/ˈrezɪdju:; US -du: ||; ˈrɛzəˌdu/noun [C] [usu.sing] (formal 正式) what is left after the main part of sth is taken or used 剩余物；残渣: The washing powder left a white residue on the clothes. 洗衣粉在衣服上留下白色残渣。

resign
/rɪˈzaɪn ||; rɪˈzaɪn/verb
1 [I,T] resign (from/as) (sth) to leave your job or position 辞去工作或职位: He's resigned as chairman of the committee. 他辞去委员会主席职位。
2 [T] resign yourself to sth/doing sth to accept sth that is unpleasant but that you cannot change 接受，忍耐（无法改变的事物）；认命: Jamie resigned himself to the fact that she was not coming back to him. 贾米只好接受她不会返回自己身边这个事实。

resignation

2 [U] the state of accepting sth unpleasant that you cannot change （对无法改变的事实的）接受；认命

resigned
/rɪˈzaɪnd ||; rɪˈzaɪnd/adj resigned (to sth/doing sth) accepting sth that is unpleasant but that you cannot change 逆来顺受的；听天由命的: Ben was resigned to the fact that he would never be an athlete. 本只好接受自己永远不会成为运动员的事实。

resilient

resin

resist
/rɪˈzɪst ||; rɪˈzɪst/verb
1 [I,T] to try to stop sth happening or to stop sb from doing sth; to fight back against sth/sb 抵抗；抗拒；对抗 · The government are resisting pressure to change the law. 政府顶住要求修改法律的压力。 [T] to resist arrest 拒捕
2 [T] to stop yourself from having or doing sth that you want to have or do 忍住: I couldn't resist telling Nadia what we'd bought for her. 我忍不住告诉纳迪亚我们给她买了什么东西。

resistance
/rɪˈzɪstəns ||; rɪˈzɪstəns/noun
1 [U] resistance (to sb/sth) trying to stop sth from happening or to stop sb from doing sth; fighting back against sb/sth 抵抗；抗拒；对抗: The government troops overcame the resistance of the rebel army. 政府军克服了叛军的抵抗。
2 [U] resistance (to sth) the power in a person's body not to be affected by disease （对疾病的）抵抗力
3 [C,U] (technical术语) (symbol R) the fact of a substance not CONDUCTINGheat or electricity (= not allowing heat or electricity to flow through it); a measurement of this 电阻；电阻率

resistant
/rɪˈzɪstənt ||; rɪˈzɪstənt/adj resistant (to sth)
1 not wanting sth and trying to prevent sth happening 抗拒的；抵抗的: resistant to change 抗拒改变
2 not harmed or affected by sth 能抵挡（某事物）的: This watch is water-resistant. 这是一只防水手表。

resistor
/rɪˈzɪstə(r) ||; rɪˈzɪstɚ/noun [C] (technical术语) a device that does not allow electric current to flow through it freely in a CIRCUIT 电阻器 ☞picture on page 987 见987页插图

resolute
/ˈrezəlu:t ||; ˈrɛzəˌlut/adj having or showing great determination 坚决的；断然的；坚定的: a resolute refusal to change 坚决拒绝改变 [SYN] Determined is more common. determined较常用。 ➔resolutely adv

resolution
/ˌrezəˈlu:ʃn ||; ˌrɛzəˈluʃən/noun
1 [U] the quality of being firm and determined 果断；坚决；坚定
2 [U] solving or settling a problem, dispute, etc （问题、争端等的）解决
3 [C] a formal decision that is taken after a vote by a group of people 决议（经投票作出的决定）: The UN resolution condemned the invasion. 联合国的决议谴责那次侵略行为。
4 [C] a firm decision to do or not to do sth 决定；决心

resolve
/rɪˈzɒlv ||; rɪˈzɑlv/verb (formal 正式)
1 [T] to find an answer to a problem 解决；解答: Most of the difficulties have been resolved. 大部份难题已经解决了。
2 [I,T] to decide sth and be determined not to change your mind 决意；决心: He resolved never to repeat the experience. 他下定决心，绝不重蹈覆辙。

resonance
/ˈrezənəns ||; ˈrɛzṇəns/noun
1 [U] (formal 正式) (used about sound) the quality of being resonant （指声音）回响，洪亮: the strange and thrilling resonance of her voice 她那古怪而又令人毛骨悚然的洪亮嗓音
2 [C,U] (technical术语) the sound produced in an object by sound of a similar FREQUENCY from another object 共振；共鸣
3 [U] [C] (formal 正式) (in a piece of writing, music, etc) the power to bring images, feelings, etc into the mind of the person reading or listening; the images, etc produced in this way （文章、乐曲等）共鸣力，共鸣

resonant
/ˈrezənənt ||; ˈrɛzṇənt/adj
1 (used about a sound 指声音) deep, clear and continuing for a long time 洪亮的；回响的: a deep resonant voice 深沉洪亮的嗓音
2 (technical术语) causing sounds to continue for a long time 激起回响的；共振的；共鸣的: resonant frequencies 共振频率
3 having the power to bring images, feelings, memories, etc into your mind 引起共鸣的: a poem filled with resonant imagery 一首充满令人共鸣的意境的诗

resonate
/ˈrezəneɪt ||; ˈrɛzəˌnet/verb [I] (formal 正式)
1 (used about a voice, an instrument, etc) to make a deep, clear sound that continues for a long time （指嗓音、乐器等）回响，回荡: Her voice resonated through the theatre. 她的嗓音在剧院里回响。
2 resonate (with sth) (used about a place) to be filled with sound; to make a sound continue longer （指地方）充满回响；使（声音）回响: The room resonated with the chatter of 100 people. 房间里回响着100个人喋喋不休的说话声。
3 resonate (with sb/sth) to remind sb of sth; to be similar to what sb thinks or believes 激起联想﹔引起共鸣: These issues resonated with the voters. 这些问题引起选民的共鸣。
resonate with sth(formal 正式) to be full of a particular quality or feeling 充满（某种特质或感情）: She makes a simple story resonate with complex themes and emotions. 她使一个简单的故事变得主题复杂、感情丰富。

resort¹
/rɪˈzɔ:t ||; rɪˈzɔrt/noun [C] a place where a lot of people go to on holiday 度假胜地: a seaside/ski resort 海滨╱滑雪度假胜地 in the last resort; (as) a last resort→LAST¹
resort²
/rɪˈzɔ:t ||; rɪˈzɔrt/verb [I] resort to sth/doing sth to do or use sth bad or unpleasant because you feel you have no choice （因别无选择而）采取，诉诸: After not sleeping for three nights I finally resorted to sleeping pills. 我三个晚上没有睡着觉，最后只得服用安眠药。

resound
/rɪˈzaʊnd ||; rɪˈzaund/verb [I] (written 书面语)
1 resound (through sth) (used about a sound, voice, etc) to fill a place with sound ﹙声音、嗓音等﹚回响，回荡: Laughter resounded through the house. 笑声在屋里回荡。 (figurative 比喻) The tragedy resounded around the world. 悲剧的反响波及全世界。
2 resound (with sth) (used about a place) to be filled with sound ﹙地方﹚回荡﹙或回响﹚着声音: The street resounded with the thud of marching feet. 街道上回荡着行进步伐的铿锵声。

resounding
/rɪˈzaʊndɪŋ ||; rɪˈzaυndɪŋ/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前)
1 very loud 响亮的；大声的: resounding cheers 大声的欢呼
2 very great 了不起的；重大的；巨大的: a resounding victory/win/defeat/success 辉煌的胜利；惨败；非凡的成功

resource
/rɪˈsɔ:s;-ˈzɔ:s; US ˈri:sɔ:rs ||; ˈrisɔrs/noun [C] [usu.pl] a supply of sth, a piece of equipment, etc that is available for sb to use 资源: Russia is rich in natural resources such as oil and minerals. 俄罗斯有丰富的天然资源，比如石油和矿物。

resourceful
/rɪˈzɔ:sfl; US -ˈsɔ:s- ||; rɪˈsɔrsfəl/adj good at finding ways of doing things 足智多谋的

*respect¹
/rɪˈspekt ||; rɪˈspɛkt/noun
1 [U] respect (for sb/sth) the feeling that you have when you admire or have a high opinion of sb/sth 尊敬；敬重；景仰；钦佩: I have little respectfor people who are arrogant. 我毫不敬重傲慢的人。 to win/lose sb's respect 赢得╱失去某人的尊敬 ☞Look at self-respect. 参看self-respect。
2 [U] respect (for sb/sth) polite behaviour or care towards sb/sth that you think is important 敬意；尊重: We should all treat older people with more respect. 我们大家都应该多尊敬老年人。 [OPP] disrespect 反义词为disrespect
3 [C] a detail or point 细节；点: In what respects do you think things have changed in the last ten years? 你认为在过去十年间事物的哪些方面有所改变呢？ Her performance was brilliant in every respect. 她的表演在各方面都很出色。
with respect to sth(formal 正式) about or concerning 关于；有关 pay your respects→PAY¹
*respect²
/rɪˈspekt ||; rɪˈspɛkt/verb[T]
1 respect sb/sth (for sth) to admire or have a high opinion of sb/sth 尊敬；敬重；景仰；钦佩: I respect him for his honesty. 我敬重他为人诚实。
2 to show care for or pay attention to sb/sth 尊重；注重；重视: We should respect other people's cultures and values. 我们应该尊重其他人的文化和价值观。 ➔respectful /-fl ||; -fəl/ adj respectful (to/towards sb) The crowd listened in respectful silence. 群众肃然静听。 [OPP] disrespectful 反义词为disrespectful ➔respectfully /-fəli ||; -fəlɪ/ adv

respectable
/rɪˈspektəbl ||; rɪˈspɛktəbḷ/adj
1 considered by society to be good, proper or correct （社会上认为）得体的，正确的，体面的: a respectable family 体面的家庭 He combed his hair and tried to look respectable for the interview. 他把头发梳理整齐，想在面试时显得得体一点。
2 quite good or large 相当好的；相当大的: a respectable salary 可观的薪酬 ➔respectability /rɪˌspektəˈbɪləti ||; rɪˌspɛktəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U]

respective

respectively
/rɪˈspektɪvli ||; rɪˈspɛktɪvlɪ/adv in the same order as sb/sth that was mentioned 依次；分别: Rhoda and Robbie, aged 17 and 19 respectively. 罗达和罗比，分别17和19岁。

respiration
/ˌrespəˈreɪʃn ||; ˌrɛspəˈreʃən/noun[U]
1 (formal 正式) breathing 呼吸
2 (technical术语) a process by which living things produce energy from food. Respiration usually needs OXYGEN. 呼吸作用（生物摄取食物产生能量）

respirator
/ˈrespəreɪtə(r) ||; ˈrɛspəˌretɚ/noun[C]
1 a piece of equipment that makes it possible for sb to breathe over a long period when he/she is unable to do so naturally 呼吸器: She was put on a respirator. 她被戴上呼吸器。
2 a device worn over the nose and mouth to allow sb to breathe in a place where there is a lot of smoke, gas, etc 防毒面具

respiratory
/rəˈspɪrətri;ˈrespərətri||; rɪˈspaɪrəˌtɔrɪ/adj connected with breathing 与呼吸有关的: the respiratory system 呼吸系统 respiratory diseases 呼吸系统疾病

respite
/ˈrespaɪt ||; ˈrɛspɪt/noun [sing] [U] respite (from sth) a short period of rest from sth that is difficult or unpleasant （在困难或不愉快的事情中的）短暂休息，暂停 [sing] There was a brief respite from the fighting. 这场战斗曾经暂时平息。

*respond
/rɪˈspɒnd ||; rɪˈspɑnd/verb[I]
1 (formal 正式)respond (to sb/sth) (with/by sth) to say or do sth as an answer or reaction to sth 回答；回复；回应；反应: He responded to my question with a nod. 他对我的提问点头回应。 Owen responded to the manager's criticism by scoring two goals. 欧文射进两个球，以响应经理的批评。 [SYN] reply 同义词为reply
2 respond (to sb/sth) to have or show a good or quick reaction to sb/sth （对某人或某事）有良好或迅速的反应: The patient did not respond well to the new treatment. 病人接受新疗法后，情况没有好转。

*response
/rɪˈspɒns ||; rɪˈspɑns/noun [C,U] (a) response (to sb/sth) an answer or reaction to sb/sth 回答；回复；反应；回应: I've sent out 20 letters of enquiry but I've had no responses yet. 我已寄出了20封询问信，但还没有收到回复。 The government acted in response to economic pressure. 政府为对付经济压力而采取行动。

*responsibility
/rɪˌspɒnsəˈbɪləti ||; rɪˌspɑnsəˈbɪlətɪ/noun (plural responsibilities)
1 [U] [C] responsibility (for sb/sth);responsibility (to do sth) a duty to deal with sth so that it is your fault if sth goes wrong 责任；职责: I refuse to take responsibility if anything goes wrong. 如果有任何事情出错，我拒绝负责。 It is John's responsibility to make sure the orders are sent out on time. 确保命令及时发出是约翰的职责。 I feel that I have a responsibility to help them -- after all, they did help me. 我觉得我有责任帮助他们，毕竟他们的确帮助过我。 Who has responsibility for the new students? 谁负责这些新生？
2 [U] the fact of sth being your fault; blame 责任；过错: No group has yet admitted responsibility for planting the bomb. 还没有哪个组织承认放置这枚炸弹是其所为。
shift the blame/responsibility (for sth) (onto sb)→SHIFT¹

*responsible
/rɪˈspɒnsəbl ||; rɪˈspɑnsəbḷ/adj
1 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) responsible (for sb/sth);responsible (for doing sth) having the job or duty of dealing with sb/sth, so that it is your fault if sth goes wrong 应负…的责任: The school is responsible for the safety of the children in school hours. 校方负责孩子们上学期间的安全。 The manager is responsible for making sure the shop is run properly. 经理有责任确保商店正常运作。
2 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) responsible (for sth) being the person whose fault sth is 应受归咎: Who was responsible for the accident? 这宗意外应归咎于谁呢？
3 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) responsible (to sb/sth) having to report to sb/sth with authority, or to sb who you are working for, about what you are doing 向…负责或交代: Members of Parliament are responsible to the electors. 国会议员要对选民负责。
4 (used about a person) that you can trust to behave well and in a sensible way （指人）可靠的，可信赖的，负责的: Marisa is responsible enough to take her little sister to school. 玛莉萨很有责任心，可以让她送她小妹妹上学。 [OPP] irresponsible 反义词为irresponsible
5 (used about a job) that is important and that should be done by a person who can be trusted （指工作）重要的，责任重大的

*responsibly
/rɪˈspɒnsəbli ||; rɪˈspɑnsəblɪ/adv in a sensible way that shows that you can be trusted 有责任感；负责可靠；理智地: They can be relied on to act responsibly. 他们做事靠得住。

responsive
/rɪˈspɒnsɪv ||; rɪˈspɑnsɪv/adj paying attention to sb/sth and reacting in a suitable or positive way 注意（某人或某事）并作出适当反应的；反应灵敏的: By being responsive to changes in the market, the company has had great success. 公司对市场动态反应灵敏，因而大获成功。

*rest¹
/rest ||; rɛst/verb
1 [I] to relax, sleep or stop after a period of activity or because of illness 休息；歇息: We've been walking for hours. Let's rest here for a while. 我们走了好几个小时的路，在这里休息一会儿吧。
2 [T] to not use a part of your body for a period of time because it is tired or painful 让（身体某部位）休息: Your knee will get better as long as you rest it as much as you can. 只要你尽量少用那边膝盖，它便会好转。
3 [I,T] rest (sth) on/against sth to place sth in a position where it is supported by sth else; to be in such a position （把某物）靠在，倚在 · She rested her head on his shoulder and went to sleep. 她把头靠在他的肩膀上，睡着了。
let sth rest to not talk about sth any longer 不再谈论（某事） rest on sb/sth to depend on sb/sth or be based on sth 依靠；基于: The whole theory rests on a very simple idea. 整个理论基于一个很简单的概念。
*rest²
/rest ||; rɛst/noun
1 [C,U] a period of relaxing, sleeping or doing nothing 休息；睡眠: I can't walk any further! I need a rest. 我再也走不动了！我需要休息一下。 I'm going upstairs to have a rest before we go out. 我上楼睡一会儿，然后我们再出去。 Try not to worry now. Get some rest and think about it again tomorrow. 现在先别担忧，稍作休息明天再想吧。 I sat down to give my bad leg a rest. 我坐下来，让我那条酸痛的腿歇一会儿。
2 the rest (of sb/sth) [sing] [with.sop] the part that is left; the ones that are left 剩余部分；其余的人或事物: We had lunch and spent the rest of the day on the beach. 我们吃过午饭后，当天剩余的时间就在沙滩上度过。 She takes no interest in what happens in the rest of the world. 她对世界上其他地方发生的事不感兴趣。 They were the first people to arrive. The rest came later. 他们最先到达，其他人后来才到。 The rest of our bags are still in the car. 我们其余的包包仍在车上。
3 [C,U] (in music) a period of silence between notes; a sign for this （音乐）休止，休止符 ☞picture at music 见music插图
at rest not moving 静止不动: At rest the insect looks like a dead leaf. 那种昆虫不动时看上去像一片枯叶子。 come to rest to stop moving 停下来；静止下来: The car crashed through a wall and came to rest in a field. 汽车撞穿一道墙壁，在一块田里停住。 put/set your/sb's mind at rest→MIND¹

restart
/ˌri:ˈstɑ:t ||; riˈstɑrt/verb [I,T] to start again, or to make sth start again, after it has stopped ﹙使﹚重新开始: to restart a game/car/meeting 重新开始游戏；再次启动汽车；重新召开会议 The doctors struggled to restart his heart. 医生竭力重新起搏他的心脏。

*restore
/rɪˈstɔ:(r) ||; rɪˈstɔr/verb [T] restore sb/sth (to sb/sth)
1 to put sb/sth back into his/her/its former condition or position 使恢复原状；使返回原位: She restores old furniture as a hobby. 她把修复旧家具作为爱好。 In the recent elections, the former president was restored to power. 最近的选举使前总统重新掌权。
2 restore sth to sb(formal 正式) to give sth that was lost or stolen back to sb 归还（遗失或被窃的物品）

restrain
/rɪˈstreɪn ||; rɪˈstren/verb [T] restrain sb/sth (from sth/doing sth) to keep sb or sth under control; to prevent sb or sth from doing sth 控制；限制；阻止；克制: I had to restrain myself from saying something rude. 我得控制自己，才不致说无礼的话。

restrained
/rɪˈstreɪnd ||; rɪˈstrend/adj not showing strong feelings 克制的；自制的

restraint
/rɪˈstreɪnt ||; rɪˈstrent/noun
1 [U] the quality of behaving in a calm or controlled way 冷静；克制: It took a lot of restraint on my part not to hit him. 我努力克制自己，才没有打他。 Soldiers have to exercise self-restraint even when provoked. 军人即使受到挑衅也要自我克制。
2 [C] a restraint (on sb/sth) a limit or control on sth 限制；约束: Are there any restraints on what the newspapers are allowed to publish? 对于报纸的内容，当局有任何限制吗？

restrict
/rɪˈstrɪkt ||; rɪˈstrɪkt/verb [T] restrict sb/sth (to sth/doing sth) to put a limit on sb/sth 限制；限定: There is a plan to restrict the use of cars in the city centre. 有一个限制在市中心使用汽车的计划。

restricted
/rɪˈstrɪktɪd ||; rɪˈstrɪktɪd/adj controlled or limited 受控制的；受限制的: There is only restricted parking available. 停车仅限若干地点。

restriction
/rɪˈstrɪkʃn ||; rɪˈstrɪkʃən/noun restriction (on sth)
1 [C] something (sometimes a rule or law) that limits the number, amount, size, freedom, etc of sb/sth 限定；限制: parking restrictions in the city centre 市中心停车的限制 The government is to impose tighter restrictionson the number of immigrants permitted to settle in this country. 政府将加强限制获准定居本国的移民人数。
2 [U] the action of limiting the freedom of sb/sth 限制；约束: This ticket permits you to travel anywhere, without restriction. 凭这张票你可以到处旅游，不受限制。

restrictive
/rɪˈstrɪktɪv ||; rɪˈstrɪktɪv/adj limiting; preventing people from doing what they want 限制的；约束性的

ˈrest room
noun [C] (US 美) a public toilet in a hotel, shop, restaurant, etc （旅馆、商店、餐馆等的）公共厕所，洗手间 ☞Look at the note at toilet. 参看toilet的注释。

restructure
/ˌri:ˈstrʌktʃə(r) ||; riˈstrʌktʃɚ/verb [T] to organize sth such as a system or a company in a new and different way 调整结构；改组 ➔restructuring noun [U,C,usually sing]: The corporation is undergoing a major restructuring. 公司正在进行重大的改组。

*result¹
/rɪˈzʌlt ||; rɪˈzʌlt/noun
1 [C] something that happens because of sth else; the final situation at the end of a series of actions 后果；结果: The traffic was very heavy and as a result I arrived late. 交通十分拥挤，因此我迟到了。 This wasn't really the result that I was expecting. 这实际上并非我所期望的结果。
2 [C,U] a good effect of an action 成果；成效；效果: He has tried very hard to find a job, until now without result. 他努力找工作，但直到现在仍毫无结果。 The treatment is beginning to show results. 这种治疗正开始见效。
3 [C] the score at the end of a game, competition or election （游戏、比赛或选举的）结果，成绩，得分: Do you know today's football results? 你知道今天足球比赛的结果吗？ The results of this week's competition will be published next week. 这星期的比赛结果将于下周公布。 The result of the by-election was a win for the Liberal Democrats. 补选的结果是自由民主党获胜。
4 [C] [usu.pl] the mark given for an exam or test （考试或测验的）分数，等级，成绩: When do you get your exam results? 你们什么时候知道考试成绩？
5 [C] something that is discovered by a medical test 医学化验结果: I'm still waiting for the result of my X-ray. 我还在等我的Ｘ光检验结果。 The result of the test was negative. 化验结果呈阴性。
result²
/rɪˈzʌlt ||; rɪˈzʌlt/verb [I] result (from sth) to happen or exist because of sth （因某事物而）发生，出现: Ninety per cent of the deaths resulted from injuries to the head. 罹难者九成因头部受伤致死。 result in sth to cause sth to happen; to produce sth as an effect 引致；导致；造成: There has been an accident on the motorway, resulting in long delays. 高速公路上发生一起事故，导致行车长时间延误。

resume
/rɪˈzu:m;-ˈzju:-; US -ˈzu:m ||; rɪˈzum/verb [I,T] to begin again or continue after a pause or interruption （暂停或中断后）重新开始，再继续，恢复: Normal service will resume as soon as possible. 正常服务将尽快恢复。

resumption
/rɪˈzʌmpʃn ||; rɪˈzʌmpʃən/noun [sing] [U] (written 书面语) beginning again or continuing after a pause or interruption （暂停或中断后的）重新开始，再继续，恢复

/rɪˈsɜ:dʒəns ||; rɪˈsɝdʒəns/noun [C] [usu.sing] (formal 正式) the return and growth of an activity that had stopped 复苏；复兴: a resurgence of interest in the artist's work 对那美术家的作品兴趣重生

resurrect
/ˌrezəˈrekt ||; ˌrɛzəˈrɛkt/verb [T] to bring back sth that has not been used or has not existed for a long time 恢复使用，使再现（很久没有使用或出现的东西）: From time to time they resurrect old programmes and show them again on television. 他们间或会在电视上回放老节目。

retake¹
/ri:teɪk ||; ˈriˌtek/verb [T] (past tense retook; past participle retaken)
1 (used especially about an army) to take control of sth such as a town again ﹙尤指部队﹚收复﹙失地﹚，恢复控制: Forces moved in to retake the city. 军队开进城市，以恢复对它的控制。 (figurative 比喻) Moore fought back to retake the lead later in the race. 后来穆尔奋力反击，重新夺回了比赛中的领先地位。

3 to take an exam or a test again, usually after failing it the first time 补考；重考

retaliate
/rɪˈtælieɪt ||; rɪˈtælɪˌet/verb [I] retaliate (against sb/sth) to react to sth unpleasant that sb does to you by doing sth unpleasant in return 报复: They have announced that they will retaliate against anyone who attacks their country. 他们已宣布会向攻击他们国家的任何人进行报复。 ➔retaliation /rɪˌtæliˈeɪʃn ||; rɪˌtælɪˈeʃən/ noun [U]: retaliation (against sb/sth) (for sth) The terrorist group said that the shooting was in retaliation for the murder of one of its members. 那个恐怖组织说，这次枪击事件是对杀害其一名成员的报复。

*retire
/rɪˈtaɪə(r) ||; rɪˈtaɪr/verb[I]
1 retire (from sth) to leave your job and stop working, usually because you have reached a certain age 退休；退职: Injury forced her to retire from professional athletics. 她因为受伤而被迫退出职业运动员生涯。
2 (formal 正式) to leave and go to a quiet or private place 退到宁静或隐蔽的地方；退隐

*retired
/rɪˈtaɪəd ||; rɪˈtaɪrd/adj having stopped work permanently 已退休的: a retired teacher 退休教师

*retirement
/rɪˈtaɪəmənt ||; rɪˈtaɪrmənt/noun
1 [C,U] the act of stopping working permanently 退休；退职: She has decided to take early retirement. 她已决定提早退休。 The former world champion has announced his retirement from the sport. 前任世界冠军宣布退出体坛。
2 [sing] [U] the situation or period after retiring from work 退休后的日子或处境 [sing] We all wish you a long and happy retirement. 我们都祝你退休后的岁月悠长，幸福快乐。
A pension is the regular money received by somebody who has retired. It comes from the government, his/her former employer or both. A pensioner or an old-age pensioner is a person who has retired because of age. 退休金叫做pension，可以由政府、雇主或者两方面支付。因年老退休而领养老金者叫做pensioner或old-age pensioner。

retrieve
/rɪˈtri:v ||; rɪˈtriv/verb[T]
1 retrieve sth (from sb/sth) to get sth back from the place where it was left or lost （在原处）取回，寻回（遗留或遗失的东西）: Police divers retrieved the body from the canal. 警方潜水员从运河中找回尸体。
2 (computing计算机技术) to find information that has been stored 检索信息: The computer can retrieve all the data about a particular customer. 计算机能将某一顾客的有关资料都找出来。
3 to make a bad situation or a mistake better; to put sth right 纠正（错误）；扭转（局面）；补救: The team was losing two-nil at half-time but they managed to retrieve the situation in the second half. 该队上半场以二比零落后，但下半场终于扭转局面。 ➔retrieval /-vl ||; -vḷ/ noun [U]

retro-
/ˈretrəʊ ||; ˈrɛtro/prefix (used in nouns, adjectives and adverbs 用于构成名词、形容词及副词) back or backwards 后；向后: retrospective 回顾的

retrograde
/ˈretrəgreɪd ||; ˈrɛtrəˌgred/adj (formal 正式) (used about an action) making a situation worse or returning to how sth was in the past （指行动）使恶化的，倒退的: The closure of the factory is a retrograde step. 关闭工厂是倒退了一步。

retrospect
/ˈretrəspekt ||; ˈrɛtrəˌspɛkt/noun in retrospect thinking about sth that happened in the past, often seeing it differently from the way you saw it at the time 回想，回顾（常与当时的看法不同）: In retrospect, I can see what a stupid mistake it was. 回想起来，我才明白当时的错误多么愚蠢。

retrospective
/ˌretrəˈspektɪv ||; ˌrɛtrəˈspɛktɪv/adj
1 looking again at the past 回顾的: a retrospective analysis of historical events 对历史大事的回顾分析
2 (used about laws, decisions, payments, etc) intended to take effect from a date in the past （指法律、裁决、款项支付等）有追溯效力的，溯及既往的: Is this new tax law retrospective? 这条新的税法有追溯效力吗？ ➔retrospectively adv

*return¹
/rɪˈtɜ:n ||; rɪˈtɝn/verb
1 [I] return (to/from...) to come or go back to a place （从某处）回来；回到（某处）: I leave on 10 July and return on 6 August. 我7月10日离开，8月6日回来。 I shall be returning to this country in six months. 我六个月内会回国。 When did you return from Italy? 你什么时候从意大利回来的？ He left his home town when he was 18 and never returned. 他18岁离开故乡，以后再没有回去。
2 [I] return (to sth/doing sth) to go back to the former or usual activity, situation, condition, etc 恢复，回复（先前或通常的活动、局面、状况等）: The strike is over and they will return to work on Monday. 罢工行动结束，他们将于星期一复工。 It is hoped that train services will return to normal soon. 希望火车服务很快就恢复正常。
3 [I] to come back; to happen again 复发；再次发生: If the pain returns, make another appointment to see me. 再疼痛的话，就再来见我。
4 [T] return sth (to sb/sth) to give, send, put or take sth back 送回；放回；归还: I've stopped lending him things because he never returns them. 他借东西从不归还，我已不再借给他了。 Application forms must be returned by 14 March. 申请表必须在3月14日之前交回。
5 [T] to react to sth that sb does, says or feels by doing, saying, or feeling sth similar 回应；回报: I've phoned them several times and left messages but they haven't returned any of my calls. 我打了好几次电话给他们，而且留下口信，但他们一次也没有回我电话。 We'll be happy to return your hospitality if you ever come to our country. 你若到我们国家来，我们会盛情款待你，报答你的殷勤招待。
6 [T] (in tennis) to hit or throw the ball back （网球）将球击回或抛回
*return²
/rɪˈtɜ:n ||; rɪˈtɝn/noun
1 [sing] a return (to/from...) coming or going back to a place or to a former activity, situation or condition 返回；回复；恢复: I'll contact you on my returnfrom holiday. 我度假回来就跟你联络。 He has recently made a return to form (= started playing well again). 他近来又恢复了状态。
2 [U] giving, sending, putting or taking sth back 送回；放回；交回: I demand the immediate return of my passport. 我要求立即发还我的护照。
3 [C] (in tennis) the act of hitting or throwing the ball back （网球）将球击回或抛回: She hit a brilliant return. 她的反击漂亮极了。
4 [C,U] (a) return (on sth) the profit from a business, etc 利润；收益: This account offers high returns on all investments. 这个账户对所有投资都提供高利润。
5 [C] (brit also 英亦作 reˌturn ˈticket) (US 美 round tripround trip ticket) a ticket to travel to a place and back again 来回票；双程票: A day return to Oxford, please. 麻烦你给我一张去牛津的即日来回票。 Is the return fare cheaper than two singles? 来回票的票价是不是要比两张单程票便宜？ [OPP] single or one-way 反义词为single或one-way
6 (also the reˈturn key) [sing] the button on a computer that you press when you reach the end of a line or of an instruction （计算机的）回车键，返回键
by return (of post) (Brit 英) immediately; by the next post （接到信之后）立即，由下一班邮递 in return (for sth) as payment or in exchange (for sth); as a reaction to sth 作为（某物的）付款；以换取（某物）；以回应（某事物）: Please accept this present in return for all your help. 请收下这份礼物，让我答谢你的帮忙。

reunion

*reveal
/rɪˈvi:l ||; rɪˈvil/verb[T]
1 reveal sth (to sb) to make sth known that was secret or unknown before （向某人）透露秘密: He refused to reveal any names to the police. 他不肯向警方透露任何名字。
2 to show sth that was hidden before 使显露；呈现: The X-ray revealed a tiny fracture in her right hand. Ｘ光显示她右手有小小骨折。

revealing
/rɪˈvi:lɪŋ ||; rɪˈvilɪŋ/adj
1 allowing sth to be known that was secret or unknown before 揭露事实的: This book provides a revealing insight into the world of politics. 这本书使人得以一窥政界的内幕。
2 allowing sth to be seen that is usually hidden, especially sb's body 暴露的（尤指身体）: a very revealing swimsuit 非常暴露的泳衣

revel
/ˈrevl ||; ˈrɛvḷ/verb (revelling;revelled (US 美) reveling;reveled) revel in sth/doing sth to enjoy sth very much 陶醉于；沉迷于: He likes being famous and revels in the attention he gets. 他喜欢出名，陶醉于受人注意的感觉。

revelation
/ˌrevəˈleɪʃn ||; ˌrɛvḷˈeʃən/noun
1 [C] something that is made known, that was secret or unknown before, especially sth surprising 被泄露或揭露的事物（尤指出人意料者）: This magazine is full of revelations about the private lives of the stars. 这本杂志内容充满了明星私生活的揭露。
2 [sing] a thing or a person that surprises you and makes you change your opinion about sb/sth 令人意想不到或耳目一新的人或事物

reveller
/revələ(r) ||; ˈrɛvḷɚ/ (US 美 reveler) noun [C] a person who is having fun in a noisy way, usually with a group of other people and often after drinking alcohol ﹙醉酒﹚狂欢者

revelry
/revlri ||; ˈrɛvḷrɪ/noun [U] (also revelries [pl]) noisy fun, usually involving a lot of eating and drinking 狂欢作乐: We could hear sounds of revelry from the house opposite. 我们从对面的房子里听到了狂欢作乐的声音。

revenge
/rɪˈvendʒ ||; rɪˈvɛndʒ/noun [U] revenge (on sb) (for sth) something that you do to punish sb who has hurt you, made you suffer, etc 报复: He made a fool of me and now I want to get my revenge. 他作弄了我，现在我想要报复。 He wants to take revenge on the judge who sent him to prison. 他想要向判他入狱的法官报复。 The shooting was in revenge for an attack by the nationalists. 这次枪击事件是为了报复民族主义者的攻击。 ☞Look at vengeance. 参看vengeance。 revenge verb [T] revenge yourself on sb She revenged herself on her enemy. 她向敌人报仇。 ☞Look at avenge. 参看avenge。

revenue
/ˈrevənju:; US -ənu: ||; ˈrɛvəˌnu/noun [U] [pl] money regularly received by a government, company, etc （政府、公司等的）收入: Revenue from income tax rose last year. 所得税的收入去年增加了。

reverberate
/rɪˈvɜ:bəreɪt ||; rɪˈvɝbəˌret/verb[I]
1 (used about a sound) to be repeated several times as it comes off different surfaces （指声音）回响，回荡: Her voice reverberated around the hall. 她的嗓音在大厅里回荡。 [SYN] echo 同义词为echo
2 reverberate (with/to sth) (used about a place) to seem to shake because of a loud noise （指地方）似被巨响震动: The hall reverberated with the sound of music and dancing. 大厅里震响着音乐声和跳舞声。

revere
/rɪˈvɪə(r) ||; rɪˈvɪr/verb [T] (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) (formal 正式)revere sb/sth (as sth) to feel great respect or admiration for sb/sth 崇敬；敬慕: He is revered as one of the greatest musicians of his generation. 他被尊崇为他那个年代最伟大的音乐家之一。

reverence
/ˈrevərəns ||; ˈrɛvərəns/noun [U] (formal 正式)reverence (for sb/sth) a feeling of great respect 敬慕；崇敬；敬重

/ˈrevərənd ||; ˈrɛvərənd/ (also reverend) adj (abbr Rev.) the title of a Christian priest 牧师，司铎（对基督教神职人员的尊称）

/ˈrevərənt ||; ˈrɛvərənt/adj (formal 正式) showing respect 恭敬的；虔敬的

reversal
/rɪˈvɜ:sl ||; rɪˈvɝsḷ/noun [U] [C] the action of changing sth to the opposite of what it was before; an occasion when this happens 彻底的改变；逆转颠倒: The government insists that there will be no reversal of policy. 政府坚称不会彻底改变政策。 The decision taken yesterday was a complete reversal of last week's decision. 昨天作出的决定与上星期的刚好相反。

*reverse¹
/rɪˈvɜ:s ||; rɪˈvɝs/verb
1 [T] to put sth in the opposite position to normal or to how it was before 使倒置；使对调: Today's results have reversed the order of the top two teams. 今天的比赛结果使为首的两队排名对调。
2 [T] to exchange the positions or functions of two things or people 使位置或功能对调: Jane and her husband have reversed roles -- he stays at home now and she goes to work. 简和她的丈夫调换了角色─现在他留在家里，她出去工作。
3 [I,T] to go backwards in a car, etc; to make a car go backwards （使车等）后退；倒（车）: It will probably be easier to reverse into that parking space. 把车倒进那个停车位大概会容易一点。 He reversed his brand-new car into a wall. 他把新买的汽车往后撞到墙上去了。
reverse (the) charges (Brit 英) to make a telephone call that will be paid for by the person who receives it 由接电话的人付电话费: Phone us when you get there, and reverse the charges. 你到达时打电话给我们，电话费由我们支付。 a reverse charge call 受话方付费电话 The American English expression is to call collect. 美国用语为call collect。
*reverse²
/rɪˈvɜ:s ||; rɪˈvɝs/noun
1 [sing] the reverse (of sth) the complete opposite of what was said just before, or of what is expected 完全相反；正好相反: Of course I don't dislike you -- quite the reverse (= I like you very much). 我当然不是不喜欢你─恰恰相反。 This course is the exact reverse of what I was expecting. 这门课程与我预期的正好相反。
2 (also reˌverse ˈgear) [U] the control in a car, etc that allows it to move backwards 倒车挡: Leave the car in reverse while it's parked on this hill. 把汽车停放在这个山坡时，要挂上倒车挡。 Where's reverse in this car? 这辆汽车的倒车挡在哪里？
in reverse in the opposite order, starting at the end and going backwards to the beginning 颠倒；逆向
*reverse³
/rɪˈvɜ:s ||; rɪˈvɝs/adj opposite to what is expected or has just been described 相反的；颠倒的 in/into reverse order starting with the last one and going backwards to the first one 逆序；以相反次序: The results will be announced in reverse order. 宣布比赛结果从最差的报起。

reversible
/rɪˈvɜ:səbl ||; rɪˈvɝsəbḷ/adj
1 (used about clothes) that can be worn with either side on the outside （指衣服）正反面都可穿的，双面式的: a reversible coat 双面式外套
2 (used about a process, an action or a disease) that can be changed so that sth returns to its original state or situation （指过程、行动或疾病）可逆的 [OPP] irreversible 反义词为irreversible

revert
/rɪˈvɜ:t ||; rɪˈvɝt/verb [I] revert (to sth) to return to a former state or activity 恢复（原来的状态或活动）: The land will soon revert to jungle if it is not farmed. 那块土地如果不用来耕种，很快会回复丛林的原貌。 If the experiment is unsuccessful we will revert to the old system. 如果这项试验不成功，我们会重新使用原来的系统。

*review¹
/rɪˈvju: ||; rɪˈvju/noun
1 [C,U] the examining or considering again of sth in order to decide if changes are necessary 重新研究、考虑、检查或评估: There will be a review of your contract after the first six months. 头六个月后公司会重新研究你的合约。 The system is in need of review. 这个系统需要检查。
2 [C] a look back at sth in order to check, remember, or be clear about sth 回顾；检讨: a review of the major events of the year 本年大事回顾
3 [C] a newspaper or magazine article, or an item on television or radio, in which sb gives an opinion on a new book, film, play, etc （报纸、杂志、电视或电台上的）评论，书评，影评，剧评: The film got bad reviews. 那部影片评论不佳。
review²
/rɪˈvju: ||; rɪˈvju/verb[T]
1 to examine or consider sth again in order to decide if changes are necessary 重新研究、考虑、检查或评估: Your salary will be reviewed after one year. 一年后，我们会再考虑调整你的薪水。
2 to look at or think about sth again to make sure that you understand it 复习；重温: Let's review what we've done in class this week. 我们来温习一下这周课上学习的内容。
3 to write an article or to talk on television or radio, giving an opinion on a new book, film, play, etc （就新书、电影、戏剧等）发表评论: In this week's edition our film critic reviews the latest films. 本周出版的一期杂志有我们影评人对最新几部影片的评论。

*revise
/rɪˈvaɪz ||; rɪˈvaɪz/verb
1 [T] to make changes to sth in order to correct or improve it 修正；修订: The book has been revised for this new edition. 本书的这个新版经过修订。 I revised my opinion of him when I found out that he had lied. 我发现他说谎以后，改变了对他的看法。
2 [I,T] (Brit 英) revise (for sth) to read or study again sth that you have learnt, especially when preparing for an exam 温习（功课）: I can't come out tonight. I'm revising for my exam. 今天晚上我不能出去。我要温习功课，准备考试。 None of the things I had revised came up in the exam. 我温习过的内容都没有考。

revive
/rɪˈvaɪv ||; rɪˈvaɪv/verb[I,T]
1 to become or to make sb/sth strong or healthy again; to come or to bring sb back to life or consciousness （使）恢复精力或健康；（使）苏醒: Hopes have revived for an early end to the fighting. 人们对战斗早日结束重燃希望。 I'm very tired but I'm sure a cup of coffee will revive me. 我累极了，但喝一杯咖啡一定可以帮我提神。 Attempts were made to revive him but he was already dead. 虽然作了抢救的尝试，可惜他已经死了。
2 to become or to make sth popular again; to begin to do or use sth again （使）复兴；再度采用或使用: Public interest in athletics has revived now that the national team is doing well. 国家代表队表现不错，大众对田径运动又开始有兴趣。 [T] to revive an old custom 恢复旧习俗

revolt
/rɪˈvəʊlt ||; rɪˈvolt/verb
1 [I] revolt (against sb/sth) to protest in a group, often violently, against the person or people in power 暴动；起义；造反；反叛: A group of generals revolted against the government. 一批将军起来造反，对抗政府。
2 [T] to make sb feel disgusted or ill 使厌恶；使作呕: The sight and smell of the meat revolted him. 那肉的样子和气味让他倒胃口。 ☞noun revulsion 名词为revulsion revolt noun [C,U] The people rose in revolt against the corrupt government. 人们奋起造反，反对腐败政府。

revolting
/rɪˈvəʊltɪŋ ||; rɪˈvoltɪŋ/adj extremely unpleasant; disgusting 使人厌恶的；令人作呕的: What a revolting colour/smell. 这种颜色╱气味真令人恶心。

*revolution
/ˌrevəˈlu:ʃn ||; ˌrɛvəˈluʃən/noun
1 [C,U] action taken by a large group of people to try to change the government of a country, especially by violent action 革命: the French Revolution of 1789 1789年法国大革命 a country on the brink of revolution 快要爆发革命的国家
2 [C] a revolution (in sth) a complete change in methods, opinions, etc, often as a result of progress （方法、见解等的）彻底改变，革命: the Industrial Revolution 工业革命
3 [C,U] a movement around sth; one complete turn around a central point (for example in a car engine) 旋转；（围绕中心）转动一周: 400 revolutions per minute 每分钟400转 ☞Look at rev ². 参看rev^2。

reˌvolving ˈdoor
noun
1 [C] a type of door in an entrance to a large building that turns around in a circle as people go through it 旋转门
2 [sing] used to talk about a place or an organization that people enter and then leave again very quickly ﹙用以表示某地方或机构人员出入或流动非常频繁﹚: The newsroom became a revolving-door workplace. 新闻编辑室里人员进出频繁。
3 [sing] used to talk about a situation in which the same events or problems keep happening ﹙用以描述同样的事或问题不断出现的局面﹚: The lack of juvenile detention facilities creates a ‘revolving door’ for young criminal suspects (they keep being arrested by the police and then released again very quickly).青少年拘留设施的缺乏使年轻的嫌疑犯们陷入了“循环活动”﹙他们不断被警方逮捕，而后又很快地被释放﹚。

rhyme¹
/raɪm ||; raɪm/noun
1 [C] a word that has the same sound as another 押韵的词；韵；韵脚

*rhythm
/ˈrɪðəm ||; ˈrɪðəm/noun [C,U] a regular repeated pattern of sound or movement 节奏: I'm not keen on the tune but I love the rhythm. 我不特别喜欢那曲调，但喜欢它的节奏。 He's a terrible dancer because he has no sense of rhythm. 他的舞跳得很差，因为他全无节奏感。 He tapped his foot in rhythm with the music. 他一只脚随着音乐打拍子。 ➔rhythmic /ˈrɪðmɪk ||; ˈrɪðmɪk/(also rhythmical /ˈrɪðmɪkl ||; ˈrɪðmɪkḷ/) adj the rhythmic qualities of African music 非洲音乐的节奏感 ➔rhythmically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

In American English go horseback riding is used. 在英国英语中，go riding是骑马游乐的常用说法：She goes riding every weekend.每个周末她都去骑马游玩。在美国英语中则用go horseback riding。

*right¹
/raɪt ||; raɪt/adj
1 correct; true 正确的；真实的: I'm afraid that's not the right answer. 那个恐怕不是正确答案。 Have you got the right time ? 你知道现在准确的时间吗？ You're quite right -- the film does start at 7 o'clock. 你说得对，影片的确是在7点开映。 You were right about the weather -- it did rain. 你对天气的预测很准确，果然下雨了。 ‘You're Chinese, aren't you?’ ‘Yes, that's right.’ “你是中国人，是吗？”“是的，没错。”
2 right (for sb/sth) best; most suitable 最好的；最合适的: I hope I've made the right decision. 我希望我所作出的决定是正确的。 I am sure we've chosen the right person for the job. 我敢肯定，这工作我们已挑了个最合适的人选。 I would help you to wash the car, but I'm not wearing the right clothes. 我很愿意帮你洗车，但我这身衣服不合适。
3 (used about behaviour, actions, etc) fair; morally and socially correct （指行为、行动等）合理的，公正的，符合道德或社会规范的: It's not right to pay people so badly. 给那么低的工资是不合理的。 What do you think is the right thing to do? 你认为怎么做才对？ [OPP] for senses 1
2and 3 wrong 第1、2及3义的反义词皆为wrong
4 healthy or normal; as it should be 健康的；正常的: The car exhaust doesn't sound right -- it's making a funny noise. 这车的排气管听起来不对劲─它发出一种很怪的声音。 I don't know what it is, but something's just not right. 我不知道出了什么问题，反正不对劲。
5 on or of the side of the body that faces east when a person is facing north 右边的: Most people write with their right hand. 大多数人用右手写字。 He's blind in his right eye. 他的右眼瞎了。 [OPP] left 反义词为left
6 (Brit 英) (spoken 口语) (used for emphasizing sth bad) real or complete （用于强调不好的事物）真正的，彻底的: I'll look a right idiot in that hat! 我戴那顶帽子活像个大笨蛋！ ➔rightness noun [U]
get/start off on the right/wrong foot (with sb)→FOOT¹ get on the right/wrong side of sb→SIDE¹ on the right/wrong track→TRACK¹ put/set sth right to correct sth or deal with a problem 纠正（某物）；处理（问题）: There's something wrong with the lawnmower. Do you think you'll be able to put it right? 这割草机坏了，你能把它修好吗？ right (you are)!(spoken 口语) yes, I will or yes, I agree; OK 好的；是: ‘See you later.’ ‘Right you are!’ “回头见。”“好的。” (as) right as rain completely healthy and normal 健康；完全正常 *right²
/raɪt ||; raɪt/adv
1 exactly; directly 正好；正是: The train was right on time. 火车十分准时。 He was sitting right beside me. 他就坐在我的身边。
2 correctly; in the way that it should happen or should be done 正确；合适: Have I spelt your name right? 你的名字我拼对了吗？ Nothing seems to be going right for me at the moment. 我目前似乎事事不顺心。 [OPP] wrong 反义词为wrong
3 all the way; completely 一直；完全: Did you watch the film right to the end? 那影片你一直看到尾吗？ There's a high wall that goes right round the house. 房子四周都有高高的围墙。
4 to the right side 向右；往右: Turn right at the traffic lights. 在交通灯处向右拐。 [OPP] left 反义词为left
5 immediately 立即；马上: Wait here a minute -- I'll be right back. 在这里等一下─我马上回来。
6 (spoken 口语) (used for preparing sb for sth that is about to happen) get ready; listen （用于请对方作好准备）预备，听着: Have you got your seat belts on? Right, off we go. 你们都系好安全带了吗？好！我们出发。
right/straight away→AWAY right now at this moment; exactly now 此刻；现在: We can't discuss this right now. 我们现在不能讨论这个问题。 serve sb right→SERVE
*right³
/raɪt ||; raɪt/noun
1 [U] what is morally good and fair 正义；正当；公正: Does a child of ten really understand the difference between right and wrong? 十岁的孩子真的会辨别是非吗？ You did right to tell me what happened. 你做得对，把这事告诉了我。 [OPP] wrong 反义词为wrong
2 [sing] the right side or direction 右边；右方: We live in the first house on the right. 我们住在右边第一幢房子。 Take the first right and then the second left. 先往右拐，再向左转。 [OPP] left 反义词为left
3 [U] [C] the right (to sth/to do sth) a thing that you are allowed to do according to the law; a moral authority to do sth （依法可有的）权利: Freedom of speech is one of the basic human rights. 言论自由是基本人权之一。 civil rights(= the rights each person has to political and religious freedom, etc) 公民权 animal rights campaigners 为动物争取权利的活动家 Everyone has the right to a fair trial. 人人都有接受公平审判的权利。 You have no right to tell me what to do. 你无权命令我做这做那。
4 the Right [sing] [with.sop] the people or political parties who are against social change 右翼人士；右翼政党
be in the right to be doing what is correct and fair 对；正确；公平: You don't need to apologize. You were in the right and he was in the wrong. 你不用道歉。你做得对，他错了。 by rights according to what is fair or correct 按理；根据公平原则: By rights, half the profit should be mine. 按理说，一半的利润应该归我。 in your own right because of what you are yourself and not because of other people 凭自己的权利、能力、实力或资格 within your rights (to do sth) acting in a reasonable or legal way 有权；合理；合法: You are quite within your rights to demand to see your lawyer. 你要求见你的律师完全合法。

ˌright of ˈway
noun (plural rights of way)
1 [C,U] (especially Brit 尤为英) a path across private land that the public may use; legal permission to go into or through another person's land （私人土地上的）公用路径；（进入或通过他人土地的）通行权: Walkers have right of way through the farmer's field. 步行者享有穿越该农民田地的通行权。
2 [U] (used in road traffic) the fact that a vehicle in a particular position is allowed to drive into or across a road before another vehicle in a different position （用于道路交通）先行权: He should have stopped -- I had the right of way. 他本该停车─我有先行权。

*ring¹

1 [C] a piece of jewellery that you wear on your finger 戒指: a gold/diamond/wedding ring 金╱钻石╱结婚戒指 an engagement ring 订婚戒指 ☞picture at jewellery 见jewellery插图
2 [C] (usually in compound nouns 通常用于构成复合名词) a round object of any material with a hole in the middle 环形物体；环；圈: curtain rings 窗帘环 a key ring (= for holding keys) 钥匙环
3 [C] a round mark or shape 圆形痕迹；圆圈: The coffee cup left a ring on the table top. 咖啡杯在桌面上留下一个圆形痕迹。 Stand in a ring and hold hands. 手拉手站成一个圆圈。
4 [C] the space with seats all around it where a performance, boxing match, etc takes place 四周设有观众席的表演场或竞技场: a circus/boxing ring 马戏表演场；拳击场
5 (US 美 burner) [C] one of the round parts on the top of an electric or gas cooker on which you can put pans 炉盘；圆形小灶盘
6 [C] a number of people who are involved in sth that is secret or not legal （从事秘密或非法活动的）一伙人，集团: a spy/drugs ring 间谍╱贩毒集团
7 [C] the sound made by a bell; the action of ringing a bell 铃声；钟声；打铃；敲钟: There was a ring at the door. 有人按门铃。
8 [sing] a ring of sth a particular quality that words or sounds have （说话的）语气；（声音的）特质: What the man said had a ring of truth about it (= sounded true). 那人说的听来似乎是真的。
give sb a ring (Brit 英) (informal 非正式) to telephone sb 打电话: I'll give you a ring in the morning. 我早上会给你打电话。
*ring²
/rɪŋ ||; rɪŋ/verb (past tense rang /ræŋ ||; ræŋ/ past participle rung /rʌŋ ||; rʌŋ/)
1 [I,T] (especially US 尤为美 call)ring (sb/sth) (up) to telephone sb/sth 打电话: What time will you ring tomorrow? 你明天什么时候打电话？ I rang up yesterday and booked the hotel. 我昨天打电话预订了旅馆房间。 Ring the station and ask what time the next train leaves. 打电话到火车站，问下一班车什么时候开。 [SYN] phone 同义词为phone
2 [I,T] to make a sound like a bell or to cause sth to make this sound （使）发出铃声: Is that the phone ringing? 是电话在响吗？ We rang the door bell but nobody answered. 我们按了门铃，可是没有人应门。
3 [I] ring (for sb/sth) to ring a bell in order to call sb, ask for sth, etc （为叫唤某人或要求某物）按铃: ‘Did you ring, sir?’ asked the stewardess. “先生，是你按的铃吗？”空中小姐问道。 Could you ring for a taxi, please? 请按铃叫一部出租车。
4 [I] (used about words or sounds) to have a certain effect when you hear them （指说话或声音）听起来有某种效果: Her words didn't ring true (= you felt that you could not believe what she said). 她的话听起来不像是真的。
5 [I] ring (with sth) to be filled with loud sounds 充满很大的声音: The music was so loud it made my ears ring. 这音乐太响，我耳朵快给震聋了。
6 [T] (past tense past participle ringed) (often passive 常用于被动语态) to surround sb/sth 包围
7 [T] (US 美 circle) (past tense past participle ringed) to draw a circle around sth （在某物周围）画个圆圈
ring a bell to sound familiar or to remind you, not very clearly, of sb/sth 听来熟悉；使想起某事: ‘Do you know Chris Oliver?’ ‘Well, the name rings a bell.’ “你认识克里斯˙奥利弗吗？”“嗯，这名字听上去熟。” ring (sb) back (Brit 英) to telephone sb again or to telephone sb who has telephoned you 覆电话: I can't talk now -- can I ring you back? 我现在不能跟你谈，我给你回电话好吗？ ring in (Brit 英) to telephone a television or radio show, or the place where you work 给电视节目、电台节目或工作单位打电话: Mandy rang in sick this morning. 曼迪今早打电话请病假。 ring out to sound loudly and clearly 发出响亮而清晰的声音

riot
/ˈraɪət ||; ˈraɪət/noun [C] a situation in which a group of people behave in a violent way in a public place, often as a protest 暴动；暴乱: Further riots have broken out in Manchester. 曼彻斯特又再爆发暴乱。 riot verb [I]: There is a danger that the prisoners will riot if conditions do not improve. 如果监狱条件没有改善，囚犯可能会闹事。 ➔rioter noun [C] run riot
1 to behave in a wild way without any control 举止狂乱或不受控制: At the end of the football match, the crowd ran riot. 足球比赛结束后，群众捣乱闹事。

rip¹
/rɪp ||; rɪp/verb (ripping;ripped)
1 [I,T] to tear or be torn quickly and suddenly （猛力）撕，撕破，扯: Oh no! My dress has ripped! 糟糕！我的连衣裙撕破了！ He ripped the letter in half/twoand threw it in the bin. 他将信撕成两半，丢进垃圾桶里。 The blast of the bomb ripped the house apart. 炸弹将房子炸开。
2 [T] to remove sth quickly and violently often by pulling it （猛力）撕，拉下，扯下: He ripped the poster from the wall. 他把海报从墙上撕下来。
rip through sth to move very quickly and violently through sth 迅速而猛烈地穿越（某物）: The house was badly damaged when fire ripped through the first floor. 大火迅速烧到二楼，房子严重受损。 rip sb off(informal 非正式) to cheat sb by charging too much money for sth 欺诈；敲竹杠 rip sth up to tear sth into small pieces 撕成碎片

*rise¹
/raɪz ||; raɪz/noun
1 [C] a rise (in sth) an increase in an amount, a number or a level （数量、数目、水平等的）增加，提高: There has been a sharp rise in the number of people out of work. 失业人数激增。 [OPP] drop or fall 反义词为drop或fall
2 [C] (US 美 raise) an increase in the money you are paid for the work you do （工资的）增加；加薪: I'm hoping to get a rise next April. 我希望四月能加薪。 a 10% pay rise 薪金加10%
3 [sing] the rise (of sth) the process of becoming more powerful or important 兴盛；崛起: The rise of fascism in Europe. 法西斯主义在欧洲的兴起 her meteoric rise to fame/power 她的迅速出名╱得势
give rise to sth(formal 正式) to cause sth to happen or exist 引起或导致某事物
*rise²
/raɪz ||; raɪz/verb [I] (past tense rose /rəʊz ||; roz/ past participle risen /ˈrɪzn ||; ˈrɪzṇ/)
1 to move upwards, to become higher, stronger or to increase 上升；提高；增加: Smoke was rising from the chimney. 烟囱冒出烟来。 The temperature has risen to nearly forty degrees. 气温已上升到将近四十度。 [OPP] fall 反义词为fall
2 (written 书面语) to get up from a chair, bed, etc 起立；起床: The audience rose and applauded the singers. 听众站起来向众歌手鼓掌。
3 (used about the sun, moon, etc) to appear above the horizon （指太阳、月亮等）从地平在线升起: The sun rises in the east and sets in the west. 太阳在东方升起，在西边落下。 [OPP] set 反义词为set
4 to become more successful, powerful, important, etc 变得更成功、强大或重要等: He rose through the ranks to become managing director. 他从普通员工晋升成为经理。 She rose to power in the 90s. 她在90年代得势。
5 to be seen above or higher than sth else 凸现
6 to come from 来自: Shouts of protest rose from the crowd. 人群中传来抗议的吶喊。
7 rise (up) (against sb/sth) to start fighting against your ruler, government, etc 起义；造反 ➔rising adj the rising cost of living 不断上升的生活费用 · a rising young rock star 声名日噪的年轻摇滚乐明星
rise to the occasion, challenge, task, etc to show that you are able to deal with a problem, etc successfully 显示能处理问题╱对付挑战╱完成任务等

*risk¹
/rɪsk ||; rɪsk/noun
1 [C,U] (a) risk (of sth/that...);(a) risk (to sb/sth) a possibility of sth dangerous or unpleasant happening; a situation that could be dangerous or have a bad result 风险；危险: Don't take any riskswhen you're driving. 驾车时可别冒险。 You could drive a car without insurance, but it's not worth the risk. 不买保险也可以开车，但不值得冒这个险。 Scientists say these pesticides pose a risk to wildlife. 科学家说，这些杀虫剂对野生生物造成危险。 If we don't leave early enough we run the risk of missing the plane. 我们若不及早动身，就可能赶不上那班飞机。 Small children are most at risk from the disease. 幼儿最受这种病的威胁。
2 [sing] a person or thing that might cause danger 有可能造成危险的人或物: If he knows your real name he's a security risk. 要是他知道你的真名，就会对你的安全构成威胁。
at your own risk having the responsibility for whatever may happen 对可能发生的事负责；自担风险；自负全责: This building is in a dangerous condition -- enter at your own risk. 这幢大楼很危险─你进去后果自负。 at the risk of sth/doing sth even though there could be a bad effect 甘冒…的风险: He rescued the girl at the risk of his own life. 他冒着生命危险把那女孩救起。
*risk²
/rɪsk ||; rɪsk/verb[T]
1 to take the chance of sth unpleasant happening 冒险: If you don't work hard now you risk failing your exams. 如果你现在不用功，考试就可能不及格。
2 to put sth or yourself in a dangerous position 使处于危险境地: The man had to risk his lifeto save the little boy. 那个人冒着生命危险救那小男孩。

*river
/ˈrɪvə(r) ||; ˈrɪvɚ/noun [C] a large, natural flow of water that goes across land and into the sea 河；河流: the River Nile 尼罗河 He sat down on the bank of the river to fish. 他在河岸边坐下来钓鱼。 A river flows into the sea. Where it joins the sea is the river mouth. A boat sails on the river. We walk, sail, etc up or down river. 河水流入(flow into)大海。与海会合的河口叫做river mouth。船在河上航行(sail on the river)，逆流而上或顺流而下可以说up／down the river。

*road
/rəʊd ||; rod/noun
1 [C] a way between places, with a hard surface which cars, buses, etc can drive along 路；道路；公路: Turn left off the main (= important) road. 向左拐离大路。 road signs 道路标志 ☞ Roads (US highways) connect towns and villages a road map of Slovakia. A road in a town, city or village that has buildings at the side is often called a street. Street is not used for roads outside towns a street map of London. A wide street, often with trees or buildings along it, is called an avenue. Motorways (US freeways / expressways) are roads with two carriageways, each with two or three lanes, that are built for traffic travelling fast over long distances, avoiding towns. A-roads are big important roads that link towns. B-roads are smaller country roads. M on a map stands for motorway. road（美国英语作highway）连接市镇和乡村：a road map of Slovakia斯洛伐克公路交通图。城镇或乡村中旁边有建筑物的道路通常叫做街道(street)。street不用于城镇外的道路：a street map of London伦敦街道图。两旁有树或建筑物的大街叫做大道(avenue)。高速公路（motorway，美国英语作freeway／expressway）有来回两条车行道(carriageway)，每条车行道有两至三条车道(lane)供快速行驶，避开城镇的长途车辆使用。Ａ级公路(A-road)是宽大而重要的道路，连接各市镇。Ｂ级公路(B-road)是较小的乡村路。地图上的Ｍ代表高速公路。
2 Road(abbr Rd) [sing] used in names of roads, especially in towns 用于道路名称（尤指市镇中的）: 60 Marylebone Road, London 伦敦玛丽莱波尼路60号
by road in a car, bus, etc 搭乘道路上的交通工具: It's going to be a terrible journey by road -- let's take the train. 乘汽车太辛苦─我们乘火车吧。 on the road travelling 在路上；在途中: We were on the road for 14 hours. 我们在路上奔波了14个小时。

*rock¹
/rɒk ||; rɑk/noun
1 [U] the hard, solid material that forms part of the surface of the earth 岩石: layers of rock formed over millions of years 经过几百万年形成的岩层 ☞picture on page 1005
2 [C] [usu.pl] a large mass of rock that sticks out of the sea or the ground （突出海水或地面的）礁石，岩壁: The ship hit the rocks and started to sink. 那艘船触礁，开始下沉。
3 [C] a single large piece of rock 巨石: The beach was covered with rocks that had broken away from the cliffs. 海滩上布满从崖上崩落的大石。
4 [C] (US 美) a small piece of rock that can be picked up; a stone 石子；石头: The boy threw a rock at the dog. 那男孩朝狗扔石子。
5 (also rock music) [U] a type of pop music with a very strong beat, played on electric guitars, etc 摇滚乐: I prefer jazz to rock. 我喜欢爵士乐多于摇滚乐。 a rock singer/band 摇滚乐歌手╱乐队 ☞Look at classical, jazz and pop. 参看classical、jazz及pop。

*roll²
/rəʊl ||; rol/verb
1 [I,T] to move by turning over and over; to make sth move in this way （使）滚动: The apples fell out of the bag and rolled everywhere. 袋里的苹果掉了出来，滚得满地都是。 He tried to roll the rock up the hill. 他想把石头推上山坡去。
2 [I] to move smoothly, often on wheels 像车轮般滚动: The car began to roll back down the hill. 汽车开始从斜坡上往后滑下去。 Tears were rolling down her cheeks. 泪珠从她的脸颊滚落下来。
3 [I,T] roll (sth) (over) to turn over and over; to make sth do this （使）打滚: The horse was rolling in the dirt. 那匹马在土里打滚。 The car rolled over in the crash. 汽车在车祸中翻了个底朝天。 We rolled the log over to see what was underneath. 我们把木头翻了个身，看看下面有什么。
4 [I,T] roll (sth) (up) to make sth into the shape of a ball or tube （把某物）卷成球形或管形 · He was rolling himself a cigarette. 他在给自己卷一根烟。 The insect rolled up when I touched it. 我一碰那昆虫，它就蜷缩起来。 [OPP] unroll 反义词为unroll
5 [T] roll sth (out) to make sth become flat by moving sth heavy over it 轧平；碾平: Roll out the pastry thinly. 把面团擀薄。
6 [I] to move from side to side 左右摇摆: The ship began to roll in the storm. 船在风暴中摇晃起来。
be rolling in money/in it(slang 俚语) to have a lot of money 腰缠万贯 roll in(informal 非正式) to arrive in large numbers or amounts 滚滚而来；涌现: Offers of help have been rolling in. 大家纷纷伸出援助之手。 roll up(informal 非正式) (used about a person or a vehicle) to arrive, especially late （指人或车辆）到达（尤指迟到）

rotate
/rəʊˈteɪt ||; ˈrotet/verb[I,T]
1 to turn in circles round a central point; to make sth do this （使）旋转: The earth rotates on its axis. 地球绕地轴自转。
2 to happen in turn or in a particular order; to make sth do this （使）轮流或按顺序发生 · We rotate the duties so that nobody is stuck with a job they don't like. 我们轮换职务﹐这样谁也不会固定在一个不喜欢的工作。

rotation
/rəʊˈteɪʃn ||; roˈteʃən/noun[C,U]
1 movement in circles around a central point 旋转；自转: one rotation every 24 hours 每24小时自转一次
2 happening or making things happen in a particular order 轮流；循环 · The company is chaired by all the members in rotation. 公司董事长由全体董事轮流担任。

rotor
/ˈrəʊtə(r) ||; ˈrotɚ/noun [C] a part of a machine that turns around a central point 机器的旋转部份: rotor blades on a helicopter 直升机旋翼

rotten
/ˈrɒtn ||; ˈrɑtṇ/adj
1 (used about food and other substances) old and not fresh enough or good enough to use （指食物或其他物质）腐烂的，变质的: rotten vegetables 烂掉的菜
2 (informal 非正式) very unpleasant 极坏的: That was a rotten thing to say! 怎么可以说这么难听的话！
3 (spoken 口语) used to emphasize that you are angry （用于强调愤怒之情）: You can keep your rotten job! 那该死的工作你就继续干吧！

rouge
/ru:ʒ ||; ruʒ/noun [U] (old-fashioned 旧) a red powder or cream used for giving more colour to the cheeks 胭脂 ☞Look at blusher. 参看blusher。

*rough¹
/rʌf ||; rʌf/adj
1 not smooth, soft or level 不平滑的；不平坦的: rough ground 高低不平的地面 [OPP] smooth or soft 反义词为smooth或soft
2 violent; not calm or gentle 粗暴的；粗鲁的: You can hold the baby, but don't be rough with him. 你可以抱这婴儿，不过别粗手粗脚的。 The sea was rough and half the people on the boat were seasick. 海上风浪很大，小船上半数的人都晕船了。 [OPP] calm 反义词为calm
3 made or done quickly or without much care; approximate 粗率的；大概的；粗略的: a rough estimate 粗略的估计 Can you give me a rough idea of what time you'll be arriving? 可以告诉我你大概什么时间到达吗？
4 (informal 非正式) looking or feeling ill （看上去或感觉）不舒服的: You look a bit rough -- are you feeling all right? 你看来有点不对劲，没什么不舒服吧？ ➔roughness noun [U]
be rough (on sb) be unpleasant or bad luck for sb （对某人来说）难堪的，不幸的
rough²
/rʌf ||; rʌf/noun in rough done quickly without worrying about mistakes, as a preparation for the finished piece of work or drawing 以草稿形式；粗略地 take the rough with the smooth to accept difficult or unpleasant things in addition to pleasant things 好坏一起承受
rough³
/rʌf ||; rʌf/adv in a rough way 粗鲁地；粗野地: One of the boys was told off for playing rough. 其中一个男孩因比赛时动作粗野而遭受申斥。 live/sleep rough to live or sleep outdoors, usually because you have no home or money 住或睡在户外（通常因无家或没钱）
rough⁴
/rʌf ||; rʌf/verb rough it to live without all the comfortable things that you usually have 过不舒适的生活: You have to rough it a bit when you go camping. 露营的时候你只好将就一些。

roughage
/ˈrʌfɪdʒ ||; ˈrʌfɪdʒ/noun [U] the types or parts of food (fibre) which help your stomach to deal with other foods 粗糙食物（多纤维质，有助消化）

roughen
/ˈrʌfn ||; ˈrʌfən/verb [T] to make sth less smooth or soft 使粗糙

*roughly
/ˈrʌfli ||; ˈrʌflɪ/adv
1 in a violent way; not gently 粗暴地；狠狠地: He grabbed her roughly by her arm. 他粗暴地抓住她的手臂。
2 not exactly; approximately 约略；大约: It took roughly three hours, I suppose. 我看大概花了三个钟头。

roulette
/ru:ˈlet ||; ruˈlɛt/noun [U] a game in which a ball is dropped onto a moving wheel that has holes with numbers on them. The players bet on which hole the ball will be in when the wheel stops. 轮盘赌

*round¹
/raʊnd ||; raυnd/adj having the shape of a circle or a ball 圆的；球形的: a round table 圆桌 in round figures/numbers given to the nearest 10, 100, 1000, etc; not given in exact numbers 以整数表示
*round²
/raʊnd ||; raυnd/adv prep ☞For special uses with many verbs, for example come round, get round , go round, etc see the verb entries. round可与许多动词连用，如come round、get round、go round等，其用法参看有关动词词条。
1 in a circle or curve; on all sides of sth 成圆圈或弧形地；在某物周围: He had a bandage right round his head. 他头上缠着绷带。 We sat round the table, talking late into the night. 我们围着桌子坐下，一直谈到深夜。 We were just talking about Ravi and he came round the corner. 我们正在谈论拉维，只见他拐过街角走来。 How long would it take to walk round the world? 绕着地球走一圈要花多少时间？ (figurative 比喻) It wasn't easy to see a way round the problem (= a way of solving it). 找出个解决问题的办法并不容易。
2 in a full circle 转一圈: The wheels spun round and round but the car wouldn't move. 车轮转了又转，汽车却一动也不动。
3 turning to look or go in the opposite direction 回头看；转去相反方向: Don't look round but the teacher's just come in. 别回头望，老师刚进来了。 She turned the car roundand drove off. 她调转车头开走了。
4 from one place, person, etc to another 由一地或人等到另一地或人: Pass the photographs roundfor everyone to see. 把这些照片传给大家看。 I've been rushing round all day. 我一整天跑来跑去。
5 in or to a particular area or place 在或到某地方: Do you live round here? 你就住在这附近吗？ I'll come round to see you at about 8 o'clock. 我8点左右来看你。
6 in or to many parts of sth 到处；向各处: Let me show you roundthe house. 让我带你四处看看这房子。 He spent six months travelling round Europe. 他花了六个月时间周游欧洲。
round about (sth) in the area near a place; approximately 在附近；在周围；大约: We hope to arrive round about 6. 我们希望6点左右到达。 the other way round in the opposite way or order 正好相反；逆序；倒置；反过来: My appointment's at 3 and Lella's is at 3.15 -- or was it the other way round? 我的约会是在3点，勒拉的在3点15分─还是倒过来？ ☞ Around has the same meaning as round and is more common in American English. around与round同义，多用于美国英语。
*round³
/raʊnd ||; raυnd/noun[C]
1 a number or series of events, etc 一连串活动: a further round of talks with other European countries 与其他欧洲国家的新一轮会谈
2 a regular series of visits, etc, often as part of a job 巡行；巡视；工作路线或区域: The postman's round takes him about three hours. 邮递员每送一回信都得花上约三个小时。 Dr Adamou is on his daily round of the wards. 阿达莫医生正在作他每天一次的病房巡视。
3 a number of drinks (one for all the people in a group) 一巡饮料（小组内人人有份）: It's my round (= it's my turn to buy the drinks). 这回我请客（该轮到我买酒了）。
4 one part of a game or competition （游戏、比赛的）回合: Parma will play Real Madrid in the next round. 下个回合比赛帕尔马队将与皇家马德里队对垒。
5 (in golf) one game, usually of 18 holes （高尔夫球）一局（通常十八洞）: to play a round of golf 打一局高尔夫球
6 a bullet or a number of bullets, fired from a gun （枪械的）一发子弹，连发射击: He fired several rounds at us. 他向我们开了好几枪。
7 a short, sudden period of loud noise 一阵短促而响亮的声音: The last speaker got the biggest round of applause. 最后一位演讲者得到最热烈的一阵掌声。
round⁴
/raʊnd ||; raυnd/verb [T] to go round sth 围绕: The police car rounded the corner at high speed. 警车高速绕过拐角。 round sth off to do sth that completes a job or an activity 使圆满结束；使完成: We rounded off the meal with coffee and chocolates. 我们喝完咖啡，吃过巧克力，那顿饭便结束了。 round sb/sth up to bring sb/sth together in one place 聚集人或物: The teacher rounded up the children. 老师把孩子聚拢在一起。 round sth up/down to increase/decrease a number, price, etc to the nearest whole number 把数字、价格等调高╱调低为整数；化成整数

2 a round platform made for children to play on. They sit or stand on it and sb pushes it round. 旋转木马 ☞picture at swing 见swing插图
3 =MERRY-GO-ROUND

rounded

2 well developed; complete and balanced 全面的；完善的；一应俱全的: a fully rounded education 非常全面的教育 She is a more rounded performer than her sister. 与她妹妹相比，她是一位更全面的演员。

*route
/ru:t; US raʊt ||; raυt/noun[C]
1 a route (from A) (to B) a way from one place to another 路线: What is the most direct route from Bordeaux to Lyon? 从波尔多去里昂走哪条路最直接？ I got a leaflet about the bus routes from the information office. 我从问讯处拿到一本关于公共汽车路线的小册子。
2 a route to sth a way of achieving sth 途径: Hard work is the only route to success. 勤劳是成功唯一途径。

*routine¹
/ru:ˈti:n ||; ruˈtin/noun
1 [C,U] the usual order and way in which you regularly do things 惯常程序；例行程序: Make exercise part of your daily routine. 要坚持每天锻炼。
2 [U] tasks that have to be done again and again and so are boring （枯燥乏味的）例行公事
3 [C] a series of movements, jokes, etc that are part of a performance （表演的）一套固定动作、笑话等: a dance/comedy routine 固定舞步；喜剧固定表演
4 [C] (computing计算机技术) a list of instructions that make a computer able to perform a particular task 例行程序
routine²
/ru:ˈti:n ||; ruˈtin/adj
1 normal and regular; not unusual or special 一般的；惯常的: The police would like to ask you some routine questions. 警方想问你一些例行问题。
2 boring; not exciting 枯燥乏味的；平淡的: It's a very routine job, really. 这件工作实在太刻板了。

routinely
/ru:ˈti:nli ||; ruˈtinlɪ/adv regularly; as part of a routine 常常；惯常地；例行地: The machines are routinely checked every two months. 这些机器每两个月进行一次例行检查。

rove
/rəʊv ||; rov/verb [I,T] (written 书面语) to travel from one place to another, often with no particular purpose 漫游；漂泊；流浪: A quarter of a million refugees roved around the country. 这个国家有二十五万难民流离失所。 bands of thieves who roved the countryside 在乡村流窜的盗贼帮

roving
/rəʊvɪŋ ||; ˈrovɪŋ/adj travelling from one place to another and not staying anywhere permanently 流动的；漂泊的；漫游的；巡回的: a roving reporter for ABC news 美国广播公司的流动新闻记者 have a roving eye (old-fashioned 旧) to always be looking for the chance to have a new sexual relationship 总是找机会寻花问柳；眼神不安分

*row¹
/rəʊ ||; ro/noun[C]
1 a line of people or things （人或物的）一行，一排: a row of books 一排书 The children were all standing in a row at the front of the class. 那些小孩在全班同学面前排成一行。
2 a line of seats in a theatre, cinema, etc （剧院、电影院等的）一排座位: Our seats were in the back row. 我们的座位在后排。 a front-row seat 前排座位
in a row one after another; without a break 接连；连续: It rained solidly for four days in a row. 雨一连下了四天。
*row³
/raʊ ||; raυ/noun
1 [C] a row (about/over sth) a noisy argument or serious disagreement between two or more people, groups, etc 争吵: When I have a row with my girlfriend, I always try to make up as soon as possible. 我跟女朋友吵嘴以后，总是设法尽快言归于好。 A row has broken out between the main parties over education. 几个大党为教育问题爆发了一场争吵。
2 [sing] a loud noise 嘈杂声: What a row! Could you be a bit quieter? 吵死了！安静点儿行吗？ row verb [I] row (with sb) (about/over sth) Pete and I are always rowing about money! 皮特跟我老是为钱争吵！

2 [T] to carry sb/sth in a boat that you row 划船载运（人或物）: Could you row us over to the island? 可以把我们划到那个小岛吗？ ☞Look at paddle. 参看paddle。 row noun [sing]
